## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a chemical concentration A, which is modeled in reaction kinetics by rate-law ordinary differential equations relating consumption/production rates to concentration and sometimes explicit time dependence (changing conditions, catalyst activity, feed/decay). With only t and A available, the most likely structures are univariate rate laws in A and optionally time-varying rate coefficients in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (A depleted linearly in time when reactant is in excess or surface-limited)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like, or pseudo-first-order)
- Second-order decay (single-species): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular 2A -> products or self-reaction)
- General n-th order power law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order fitting)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating with limiting reagent or carrying-capacity-like constraint)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium (linearized): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (first-order approach to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Reversible with conserved total pool: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A) (forward/backward with total c2)
- Inhibited (substrate inhibition / deactivation) rational rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate saturates/weakens at high A or limited active sites)
- Strong inhibition (Hill-type inhibition without explicit Hill naming): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A**c1 + c2) (higher-order inhibition/aggregation effects)
- Time-varying first-order coefficient (exponentially changing conditions): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (rate constant drifting due to heating/cooling or catalyst activation)
- Catalyst/activity decay causing slowing rate: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (decreasing effective k over time, e.g., catalyst poisoning)
- Linearly drifting rate coefficient: dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + t) * A (approximately linear change in k with time over limited window)
- Decreasing availability with time (e.g., catalyst deactivation) rational-in-time: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + t) (effective rate decreases like 1/t scaling)
- Mixed-order (parallel pathways): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous unimolecular and bimolecular consumption)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Consumption vs production sign: predominantly negative dA_dt over t indicates net consumption; positive terms suggest formation or back-reaction contributions
- Reaction order inference: linear dependence on A implies first-order; curvature on log(-dA_dt) vs log(A) suggests power-law order A**n
- Equilibrium/steady-state attraction: factors like (A - c) or (c - A) imply relaxation to a stable fixed point at A = c
- Autocatalysis recognition: presence of A multiplied by (c - A) indicates self-acceleration at low A with slowdown near depletion/limit
- Parallel-pathway signature: sums of different powers (A and A**2) indicate multiple mechanisms contributing concurrently to dA_dt
- Inhibition/limited-site behavior: rational forms A/(A + c) or A/(A**n + c) indicate diminishing marginal rate at high A due to inhibition, crowding, or finite active sites
- Time-dependent rate constants: multiplicative exp(c*t), (t + c), or 1/(t + c) factors imply environmental drift (temperature, mixing) or catalyst activation/deactivation over time
- Conserved-pool/reversibility: terms like -k1*A + k2*(c - A) indicate forward/backward exchange within a fixed total amount c
- Finite-time depletion check: zero-order (-c0) predicts linear depletion reaching A=0 in finite time; higher-order laws generally slow down as A decreases
- Mechanistic plausibility constraint: for closed systems without feed, dA_dt should approach 0 as A approaches 0 for orders >= 1; a nonzero intercept at A=0 suggests external source/sink or mis-specified baseline
